Total Withdrawal of Japanese Soldiers Stationed Beyond Borders; Restored to the State of September 30th 80

According to the Central News Agency, the Japanese Naval Landing Forces stationed in Shanghai had been intensifying their positions along North Szechuan Road since 4:20 AM on the 1st, adding checkpoints and installing barbed wire, creating a very tense situation. It is now learned that this situation was completely relaxed as of 4:20 AM yesterday, and the state of affairs has been restored to that of September 30th. In the past 48 hours, the tense situation caused public anxiety. According to the Japanese side, the 48-hour alert was purely due to the sentencing in the Zhongshan case, fearing unexpected events. Yesterday morning, reporters patrolled the North Szechuan Road area. "Except for five locations - the intersections of Kiangwan Road, Tihua Road, Sze Da Road, and Scott Road, the end of the road, and the Tientungan Railway Station - where four armed Japanese soldiers were stationed at each, the rest had been withdrawn to the military camp. Some of the military telephones that had been installed the day before had also been removed. At the intersections of Yongfeng Building, Chapoo Road, and Haining Road, although armored vehicles were still parked in front of the Japanese military outposts, they were no longer seen moving around. As for the urban areas, such as Hujia Wood Bridge, Tiantong Road Bridge, Linping Road Bridge, Qimei Road Bridge, Shajing Port Bridge, Bao'an Road, Jixiang Road intersection, Bao'an Road intersection, Qimei Road, Quanjia'an Road intersection, and the east end of Xiangde Road, where Japanese soldiers had been stationed in the past two days, they had also all been withdrawn as of yesterday morning. As a result, rumors in the city gradually subsided, and people's minds became more at ease. It is also learned that the situation of the Japanese troops in the Japanese brewery behind the Sixth Third Garden and in the Ouyang Road Japanese Elementary School remained the same. However, it is learned that a new watchtower has been built at the Japanese military outpost at 1097 Tihua Road.

According to the New Voice News Agency, the Hongkou and Zhabei areas yesterday were generally more relaxed than the day before, and had largely returned to the state before September 30th. The Japanese military's expanded deployment was merely a show of force due to the Zhongshan Hide male case. Now that the case has been adjudicated and the Japanese side is satisfied, the New Voice News Agency reporter, while passing by the Japanese Naval Landing Forces headquarters on Jiangwan Road yesterday, saw red paper similar to slogans posted on the wall on the right side, with words such as "Zhongshan Hide male case adjudicated," seemingly an expression of satisfaction. The Japanese military's deployment in the concession areas, which began on the 1st, extended south from North Szechuan Road and Laobaidu Road to Suzhou Road and the Suzhou Creek bank. Except for the barbed wire at each key intersection, which was removed early in the morning the day before, the stationed posts were also completely withdrawn as of 4:30 AM yesterday. The area of patrol is still limited to Laobaidu Road; north of Laobaidu Road, it remains the same as usual. However, the number of posts and formations of skirmishers or vehicle patrols seems to have decreased as well. The same is true for the area around Wusong Road, Haining Road, and Peng Road. In Zhabei, the eastern part, such as East Sports Association Road, Ouyang Road, Sze Da Road, Xiangde Road, Scott Road, Qimei Road, Tihua Road, Baoxing Road, Kiangwan Road, Tiantong Road, Tiantong Road Bridge, Old Cigarette Bridge Road, Cigarette Bridge, and Shajing Port Road, where Japanese military posts were densely deployed the day before and the situation was quite serious, also tended to be calm yesterday. The Japanese military posts were also completely withdrawn at 4:30 AM yesterday morning. However, skirmishers or formations of vehicles were still patrolling. The western part, such as Jiangwan Road, Tongji Road, and Hengye Road, which had already been relatively peaceful the day before, became even better yesterday. However, at the intersection of Jiangwan Road and Tongji Road and in Hengye Road and other places, the Japanese military, under the pretext of protecting Japanese students, sent several posts around 7:00 AM yesterday morning, which were withdrawn around 8:30 AM; they went again at 11:30 AM and withdrew around 1:00 PM in the afternoon, after which they did not send any more. But like other places, there were still patrol teams coming and going. As for the open space at the end of Garden Street behind the Sixth Third Garden, when the reporter went there around 10:00 AM yesterday morning, he happened to see more than a hundred Japanese soldiers, divided into three or four teams, either scattered or gathered, or rising and falling, apparently drilling. The area around the Japanese cemetery at Eight Character Bridge was also very peaceful.

Chinese Suspected

According to the North China Daily News, at 10:00 AM the day before (the 2nd), a Chinese man surnamed Liu, who had arrived in Shanghai from the interior, was detained by Japanese sailors at Gujia Wood Bridge in Zhabei and taken to the Naval Landing Forces headquarters. However, he was released shortly after. According to the Japanese sailors, the Chinese man had been staring at them incessantly, and they feared there was danger, so they detained him. However, according to Liu, he was detained while he and others were reading a notice from the Public Security Bureau.

German Detained

According to the North China Daily News, at around 5:15 PM the day before (the 2nd), a German named Jordan, carrying a camera, was walking to the corner of Miller Road and Peng Road when he was about to photograph sailors unloading ammunition. Japanese sailors stationed on Miller Road saw him, immediately approached, surrounded him, and escorted him to the temporary defense post of the Japanese Naval Landing Forces on Miller Road. Those inside the defense post discussed for a long time. Jordan, unable to speak Japanese, did not say a word. Half an hour later, Jordan wanted to leave the defense post but was stopped by two sentries at the door. At this time, the Hongkou Police Station had already been informed, and several Western police sergeants arrived at the post by car, stating that Jordan had not taken any pictures. Thereupon, they handed Jordan over to them, and after a Western detective questioned him and clarified the situation, he was released.

American Reports

According to the North China Daily News, the North China Daily News reporter, American Miss Meslin, who was detained by Japanese sailors at the Japanese Naval Landing Forces headquarters on Tuesday, has already reported in detail to the US Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Gauss, yesterday. Gauss, after listening, said that he would continue to investigate the matter and was unable to say whether he would lodge a protest with the Japanese authorities. It is noted that Meslin, after returning to the North China Daily News office that day, immediately notified Gauss by telephone and went to the US Consulate General yesterday morning to report everything in detail.

Bullet Grazes Hotel

According to the North China Daily News, at around 4:30 PM the day before (the 2nd), a Japanese sailor who was off duty was walking on Nansun Road when, unexpectedly, a bullet from his rifle was discharged, grazing the roof of a tavern owned by an American named Alexander across the street. The owner had served in the European War for several years and strongly opposed Japanese sailors pointing their fingers at the triggers of their rifles when patrol teams passed in front of his tavern. Yesterday, after the stray bullet grazed the roof of his tavern, he was even more enraged, as his family was upstairs in the room at the time.

Japanese Residents Demand

According to the North China Daily News, the Diplomatic Committee of the Japanese Residents Association has resolved to urge the Association to find ways to increase the number of Japanese plainclothes detectives in the Public Concession. As for the suggestion of appointing Japanese to be the chief detectives of the Tihua Road and Yangtzepoo Road police stations, it has been temporarily shelved pending further thorough investigation. It is noted that the Japanese Road Association also sent a letter to Mr. Fessenden, Director-General of the Municipal Council, on September 28th, making the same request, stating that adopting this plan would increase the effectiveness of police protection.

War Insurance Prices Increase

A reporter from the Datong News Agency inquired with the insurance industry yesterday and learned the reason for the increase in war insurance prices. Since the Tianport case, the situation in this port has been serious. Although war insurance for the Zhabei district cannot be insured, the war insurance premium has increased from one yuan and several dimes per thousand yuan to seven yuan and fifty dimes. This is indeed true.

Shanghai Market: Rice Prices Soar, but Rice Supply Remains Abundant 82

According to the Dagu News Agency, recently, residents of this city, in view of the increasingly serious situation between China and Japan, are purchasing grain in preparation for food and taking precautions, regardless of large or small households, to prevent any eventuality. Therefore, rice sales have increased sharply, and rice prices have risen by forty or fifty cents per picul since the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning, there was still a tendency for prices to continue to rise in the market. The current price of first-grade white rice is eleven yuan and forty or fifty cents, new rice is about ten yuan and eight or nine cents to eleven yuan and one dime, second-grade rice is all within ten yuan, and the next grade is between eight and nine yuan.

River Rice Congestion

In the past week, the demand in Shanghai has surged. River rice from various areas in the interior, such as Changshu, Wuxi, Suzhou, Tongli, Sijing, Kunshan, Zhangyan, Fengjing, Jiashan, Zhenze, Xitang, Lili, Qingpu, Liyang, Zhitang, and Shuangfeng, is being transported to Shanghai in large quantities. The rice industry wharves north and south of the Suzhou Creek and Huangpu River are extremely congested with ships. The daily supply reaches more than 10,000 piculs, and the rice carried by each ship can be completely unloaded within two or three days.

Total Rice Stock

A reporter from the Dagu News Agency investigated the rice market yesterday morning. The total amount of rice in stock in the city is estimated to be more than 200,000 piculs of Kehsien rice and 130,000 to 40,000 piculs of new and old white rice produced in various counties in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, totaling more than 360,000 piculs, which is sufficient for the city's residents to consume for more than a month. At present, the number of Kehsien rice transshipped from Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi and other places to Shanghai is also very large, and the new late rice and new japonica rice in the country will soon be on the market one after another. There is absolutely no fear of food shortages in the country.

Japanese Purchasing Rice

As for the Japanese side, Mitsui & Co. and Mitsubishi & Co. have jointly formed a grain transportation company to purchase old rice and new japonica rice in the interior of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. It is reported that the first batch of goods has been loaded and exported, and they are still continuing to purchase and hoard. The Japanese purchase of our country's rice is undoubtedly for military preparations.

Newly Appointed Ambassador to the United States: Wang Zhengting Returns to China from Europe Yesterday and is Scheduled to Enter Beijing in a Day or Two to Pay Respects to the Authorities 83

According to the Central News Agency, the newly appointed ambassador to the United States, Wang Zhengting, led our World Games delegation and arrived in Shanghai by the Italian postal ship Conte Rosso at 1:00 PM yesterday. Those who went to welcome him included Li Dachao, the representative of Mayor Wu, Zhou Jue, the director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Wang Zhinan, the secretary of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, Zhu Changnian, the superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and many others such as Liu Yunfang and Fan Guang. Wang met with reporters in shifts on the ship and gave a speech, stating briefly: "I have been abroad for four months this time, first to the United States and then to Germany. There will be separate reports on the experience of participating in the World Games. Recently, the relationship between China and Japan has been quite tense. I had heard about it while in Europe, but not in great detail. The situation in Europe is that the entire continent is uneasy and restless due to the Spanish Civil War, so there is no time to look east. The only way out for our country at present is to unite, support the government, concentrate our strength, and unify our steps to seek the survival of our nation. This time, the Guangdong-Guangxi issue was resolved peacefully, and national unification was declared complete. European and American countries have greatly praised this. As I have been ordered to be an envoy to the United States, I will naturally work hard to promote the friendship between China and the United States. I will be entering Beijing in a day or two to meet with Minister Zhang, ask for instructions on matters related to going abroad, and also intend to meet with President Jiang to ask for instructions on everything."

Xue Guangqian Talks About His Return from Overseas Studies: Various Countries Are Striving to Prepare for Wartime Economy; Our Country Should Start with Sound Organization 84

According to the New Voice News Agency, Mr. Xue Guangqian went abroad in the spring of the year before last. He was sent by the former Rural Rehabilitation Committee of the Executive Yuan as a special commissioner to study rural economies in Europe. After arriving in Europe, Xue realized that while rural economy is indeed an important foundation for establishing a country, national defense economy is even more fundamental to establishing rural economy. Therefore, in addition to his research, he stayed in Italy and entered the Royal University of Rome to study national defense economy under the world-renowned financial scholar Mr. Stefanini for two years, gaining considerable experience. He was awarded a doctorate by the university and received much praise. Before returning to China, Xue also went to various European countries to investigate everything. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday with his wife on the Conte Rosso. The New Voice News Agency reporter, believing that national defense economy is important and that the number of people in our country studying this subject is still small, specifically sought an interview to inquire about everything. Mr. Xue replied,

"The scope of national defense economy is very broad. In short, in peacetime, it is nothing more than controlled economy, and in wartime, it is war economy. At present, the international situation is tense, and various countries are eager to prepare for war economy, fearing that they will be too late. Our country is facing national difficulties, and we should not ignore this. The preparation of various countries for war economy is the initial step of economic mobilization, and also the preparation for the transition from peacetime economy to war economy. The general principle is nothing more than seeking to suit and balance the supply and demand of national manpower, talent, and resources. Therefore, at present, countries are striving to increase the amount of female labor in terms of population and using railways to adjust the density of the population. In terms of finance and finance, they are preventing the escape of funds, controlling international exchange rates, issuing war bonds, and increasing taxes, etc. In terms of transportation and communication, they are striving to establish wireless communication networks, increase berths and docks, expand air traffic, and build wartime railways and highways. In terms of industry, they are striving for standardization, technicalization, and mechanization, using machines to replace labor and achieve mass production. In terms of agriculture, they are paying attention to the establishment of permanent profits, large-scale farming, and research on substitutes. In terms of resources, they are striving for the safety of resource areas, the acquisition of resource-supplying countries, and the storage and development of raw materials. In short, it is necessary to make the various parts of the peacetime economy form a new situation to adapt to the various changes that occur in wartime. At present, countries are working tirelessly on this kind of work, which is actually a declaration of preparedness for war.

For example, Italy's national economy, no matter how small a matter or thing, is controlled by the Ministry of Economic Cooperation, and everything is adapted to the dynamics of wartime. The reason why it can be like this is actually due to the strict organization of national industrial and commercial groups. The whole of Italy is organized by government-appointed personnel into 22 industrial cooperatives, bringing together consumers, sellers, producers, and even suppliers of raw materials to discuss and cooperate with each other to seek the average development of the industrial economy. There are also nine major trade associations for agriculture, industry, commerce, banking, insurance, and freelance professions, with separate organizations for labor and management to adjust the interests of labor and management and to seek the improvement of the overall national economy. And each group has designated cadres in economic mobilization to take charge of its affairs, closely liaise with the Ministry of Economic Cooperation, so that the government commands the whole country as one person, as easy as using an arm, and can allocate resources freely. Our country is in an unprecedented difficulty in history, with nine deaths and one life, cutting clothing and saving food, relying on our own efforts and regenerating ourselves. War economy cannot be formed overnight and must be prepared quickly in order to achieve something. And the most important thing for preparation is to

improve the organization, especially the organization of industrial and commercial groups, otherwise, people will be selfish and each will calculate for himself, and everything will be difficult to concentrate. Without concentration, how can we control it? It was previously heard that the Chamber of Commerce in this city, in order to amend the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Industrial and Commercial Guild Law, requested the legislative authorities to stipulate that the same industry must join the guild, which is an important plan to improve the organization. However, based on the government's legislative intention, it seems difficult to give mandatory provisions to the people's freedom of association, so the numerous requests of commercial groups over the years have not been given clear provisions. However, referring to the organizational rules of Italian industrial and commercial groups, joining the association is voluntary, but those who do not join the association must, in accordance with national laws and regulations, bear the same obligations as members to pay membership dues and abide by all group contracts. At the same time, the rights granted to members by the government cannot be enjoyed by non-members. In this way, the state has not mandatory stipulated membership, but merchants, because of the balance of rights and obligations, are happy to join, so in practice it is no different from mandatory. All these vivid applications of legislative policy are sufficient to serve as a reference." It is heard that during Xue's study in Europe, he also held a position in the Embassy in Italy and was relied upon by the Ambassador to Italy, Liu Wendao. This time, he was called back to China by Minister Zhang of the Ministry of Railways and will serve in the Ministry. Therefore, after Xue arrives in Shanghai, he will immediately enter Beijing to pay his respects to the authorities, report everything, and then take up his duties in Beijing.

Page 10

Song Ziliang Speaks Freely on the Financial and Financial Conditions of Guangdong Province: Implementing Prohibition of Gambling and Abolishing Harsh Taxes to Relieve the People's Suffering; Guangdong Province's Silver Dollar Reserve Has Been Substantially Replenished According to Law 85

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, Song Ziliang, the special financial commissioner and director of the Department of Finance of Guangdong Province, flew from Guangdong to Shanghai by China Aviation on the 30th because he had to report to Minister Kong on the current financial situation of Guangdong Province and handle matters concerning the China Construction Company and the National Products Bank. A reporter from the Xin Xin News Agency went to visit him and inquired about the financial and financial problems of Guangdong Province. According to Song, everyone knows about the past chaos in Guangdong's finances. When I went to Guangdong to take office, the whole province had just been laid, and the financial situation was like a mess, and I felt that there were thousands of things to do and I didn't know where to start. Since February, I have been implementing the central government's rectification policy step by step, and with the assistance of the elders of the province, the progress has been quite rapid, and the initial rectification work has come to an end. The most significant work is to implement the prohibition of drugs and abolish harsh taxes to relieve the suffering of the people of Guangdong over the years. However, after this rectification, the income from gambling and harsh taxes has been reduced by no less than tens of millions of yuan. Furthermore, we have vigorously practiced frugality and reduced redundant agencies and floating personnel as much as possible. Except for the educational and cultural expenses, which have been increased appropriately, we have tried our best to reduce expenditures to seek a balance between income and expenditure. The progress of the change to the Silver Dollar system is also quite smooth. Now that the ratio of the Silver Dollar to the legal tender has been set, the financial market has been very stable, and commerce has become more active as a result. The total amount of Silver Dollar issued is more than 24.9 million yuan, with a total of 60% cash reserve. The shortage is 17% more. And the 40% guarantee reserve is not accurate. In addition to the central government's restructuring of the 120 million yuan of financial public bonds in Kwangtung Province, which has made up the reserve, the Ministry of Finance has also discussed with the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Bank of China to prepare cash and transport it to Kwangtung as a reserve, so the Silver Dollar reserve has been substantially replenished according to law. The unification of the national currency system has been completed, and the financial and financial situation of Kwangtung Province will inevitably become better and better in the future. This is indeed something to tell the people of the country. Song also said at the end that Kwangtung had previously borrowed 2 million yuan from the Shanghai banking community to control the specialty of native tobacco and will use the funds to provide loans to tobacco farmers to relieve the tobacco farmers from the exploitation of tobacco merchants.

Protection of Animals Society: Holding a Life-Protecting Campaign Today; Special Document and Art Exhibition Held Yesterday and Today; Animal Treatment Center to be Established and Regulations to be Drafted 87

Today is World Animal Day, with a city-wide ban on slaughter for the day. The Chinese Society for the Protection of Animals, to promote the movement of protecting life, has specially designated yesterday and today to hold an exhibition of life-protecting writings and paintings from all levels of schools in the city at the City Chamber of Commerce to promote awareness. Visitors are very enthusiastic. The Society, out of compassion for the suffering of sick animals, is also establishing an animal treatment center. Details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Exhibition: Purpose

The Chinese Society for the Protection of Animals, to promote the movement of life-protecting, is holding an exhibition of essays and books solicited from all levels of schools in the city at the City Chamber of Commerce in the Temple of the Queen of Heaven. The Chairman of the Society, Ye Gongchuo, specially issued a statement on the purpose of the exhibition, saying, "Some may say that in these troubled times of global affairs and changing circumstances, promoting the protection of life instead of engaging in practical work is contrary to the times." I say, "It seems so, but it is not." Although there are various underlying political causes for international wars, they are actually facilitated by a few warmongers. Regardless of who the culprit is, the ultimate victory will belong to those who have construction and production in the rear. This can be asserted. The matter of protecting animals, viewed superficially, may not directly contribute to the current crisis in our country, but it is actually one of the most crucial tasks in the construction of people's hearts. In recent times, the social customs have deteriorated, and morality has declined. The promotion of the Eight Virtues of the New Life Movement is also a wake-up call to awaken those who are lost in their dreams. Guan Zhong said, "There is no sorrow greater than the death of the heart." Even if a country's weakness reaches its extreme, if the people's hearts are not dead, it can ultimately be recovered. Moreover, war is a momentary phenomenon, while construction is the foundation of a nation for ten thousand years. Therefore, since the establishment of this Society, it has been three years in an instant. Over the years, it has stood against all opinions, adhering to the principles of the sages, treating all beings as one's own, and nurturing all life together, diligently working on publicity to revitalize the decadence of people's hearts. Fortunately, it has received sympathy and support from all parties, and the Society's affairs have progressed day by day. This year, it is holding an exhibition of life-protecting writings and paintings from all levels of schools in the city, hoping that our country's inherent benevolence, universal love, and ancient virtues will be deeply imprinted in the minds of children so that pure hearts can retain good images early on. Dr. Sun Yat-sen said, "Revolution requires revolution of the heart first." The meaning of protecting animals is such. However, this matter is of great importance, and our efforts are limited. We still rely on the generosity of gentlemen at home and abroad to help us."

Exhibition: Situation

The exhibition of life-protecting writings and paintings from all levels of schools opened at 9 a.m. yesterday. Visitors streamed in an endless flow. From the gate of the City Chamber of Commerce, along both sides of the corridor, were plastered slogans and paintings promoting the protection of life, which could not help but evoke compassion for animals. The exhibition of writings and paintings was set up in the main hall of the Chamber of Commerce. The materials provided by the schools were extremely rich, and many were masterpieces, with more than a thousand items in total, a dazzling array that was a feast for the eyes. The Society sent many staff members to take care of the venue, and the Boy Scouts from Renhui Elementary School helped to maintain order. It is expected that today, being Sunday, there will be even more visitors. The Society welcomes visitors from all walks of life. However, the gift department requires a visiting pass issued by the Society to show restrictions.

Animal Treatment

The Society, to provide practical relief and alleviate the suffering of sick animals, plans to establish an animal treatment center. The following is a record of its origins: "Announcing that this Society has recently observed that various mute animals serve humans all day long, and their bodies have already suffered great pain. Once they develop diseases or injuries, they cannot speak and have no medical treatment, and their miserable groans are unbearable to witness. To provide practical relief and alleviate their suffering, we plan to actively establish an animal treatment center. Animals such as cattle, horses, sheep, dogs, cats, rabbits, chickens, and geese, when they develop diseases or injuries to their limbs, can be reported to this Society or sent to the center for free treatment, so that countless animals with the same spirituality can enjoy equal treatment. However, this matter is of great importance and requires sufficient financial resources to succeed. In addition to having hired all the faculty and students of the Shanghai Gongli Veterinary College as veterinarians, we plan to appeal to benevolent people at home and abroad to uphold the grand vision of treating all things as one and practicing great compassion and kindness, to contribute generously and provide continuous support. Donations, regardless of size, will be equally meritorious, and the gratitude will not be limited to animals."

Request to Enact Regulations

Yesterday, the Society specially submitted a request to the Legislative Yuan to enact regulations prohibiting cruelty to animals. The original submission stated, "Regarding the protection of animals, most European and American countries have established laws that have been implemented for a long time and have shown increasing effects. Recently, some have even included them in their constitutions. Their benevolence and righteousness are widely known and emulated everywhere. Our country was civilized the earliest, and the people have always cherished benevolence and love. Treating all things as one's own has been a clear teaching since ancient times. However, in recent times, people's hearts have become callous, and cruel customs have become increasingly rampant. Some indulge in satisfying their appetites, while others seek the benefits of exploitation, not hesitating to use all kinds of cruel methods on defenseless animals, causing injuries all over the place, which is shocking to witness. According to Article 21 of the current Implementation Rules of the Hunting Law of our country, 'Local authorities may, according to local conditions, formulate regulations to protect beneficial animals, which shall be implemented in conjunction with the Hunting Law and these Implementation Rules.' However, in reality, local authorities have not formulated the aforementioned regulations for the protection of beneficial animals, and the original intention of the legislation cannot be implemented. When facts occur, officials at all levels often use the excuse of not having laws to rely on, and do not prohibit them, or even regard them as remote and ridiculous. This deeply worries about hindering the rescue of people's hearts and the suppression of hostility, and the Society's work feels even more unable to proceed. Therefore, we have excerpted and translated the articles of the British Hunting Law and examples of cruelty to animals, and sent them to your esteemed Yuan, requesting that articles prohibiting cruelty to animals be stipulated in any law, whether it is of a positive nature, or that separate regulations prohibiting cruelty to animals be enacted to supplement the deficiencies of the current law. We respectfully await your esteemed Yuan's decision and implementation, which would be fortunate for all beings. This is submitted to Sun, the President of the Legislative Yuan, by Ye Gongchuo, Chairman of the Chinese Society for the Protection of Animals, and Guan Jiongzhil, Vice Chairman."

Rescuing Cats and Dogs

The Continental Daily News reports that the Shanghai Society for the Prevention of Cruelty to Animals has prepared a cat and dog ambulance that patrols the roads every day. Injured or sick cats and dogs are taken to the veterinary hospital for treatment. However, lost cats and dogs should still be handled by the police and will not be interfered with. Yesterday, the ambulance was on the streets for the first day and rescued a dog on Avenue Joffre that had been run over by a passing car. Today is the Society's annual fundraising day, and it is hoped that 5,000 yuan can be raised to cover the working expenses for the coming year. It is reported that the Society is organized by foreigners living in Shanghai and has more than a hundred members, with many Chinese women providing support.

Shipping Accidents: Incidents on the Jianghai Sea Routes 88

"Fuhua" Carelessness

The "Fuhua" steamship of the Sanbei Company, which operates between Chongqing and Yichang, was transferring cargo bound for Sichuan from the company's "Little Sanbei" steamship on the 26th of last month. At 6 p.m., workers began loading cargo at the Yichang wharf. Several barrels of gasoline, salvaged from the stranded "Fuyang" steamship, were loaded on the front deck of the "Fuhua." It was said that there were some private goods (carried privately by people on the ship). One of the barrels leaked, and gasoline spilled onto the deck. Unexpectedly, a loading worker mistakenly threw cigarette ash onto the oil, causing a sudden burst of flames. With a loud explosion, the oil barrel exploded, killing two workers on the deck instantly. More than twenty others were injured (light burns). The remaining fire was extinguished, and the injured were sent to the hospital. The deaths were reported to the authorities and inspected by the court on the 27th. The corpses were collected and put in coffins. At the time of the explosion, the hull and internal machinery of the ship were not damaged. One cabin on the deck was destroyed. On the 27th, the cargo was loaded, and the ship sailed to Shashi, and after unloading the cargo in Chongqing, it will come to Shanghai for repairs.

"Huaping" Aground

The "Huaping" steamship of the Minxin Company, which originally sailed between Xinghua and Quanzhou, has recently changed its route to Haizhou to load salt and transport it to the Yangtze River due to the off-season. Yesterday, the company received a telegram from the owner of the "Huaping" steamship, stating that the ship had run aground at Chenjiagang, west of Kwangshan, due to shallow water. The ship's draft was more than 17 feet. It is now waiting for the tide and trying to rescue the ship. Details have not yet been reported to Shanghai. The Minxin Company has sent a telegram to inquire.

"Litong" Steamship Encountered Danger at Sea 89

The "Litong" steamship of the Huitong Shipping Company, with a deadweight of 1,854 tons, a length of 27.5 feet, a width of 5.6 feet, a depth of 28.6 inches, and a draft of 22.5 inches, has 800 horsepower and can travel 12 nautical miles per hour. The ship was built in 1884. It was fully loaded with cargo and sailed from North China. On the afternoon of the first of this month, the ship was sailing in

Korean Waters

near Incheon, at 135 degrees 05 minutes east longitude and 37 degrees 17 minutes north latitude. According to the nautical chart, the location was near Nanao. The ship was proceeding when a strong wind suddenly arose at sea. The ship was hit by the strong wind and waves, making it impossible to move forward. However, the ship was sailing head-on into the wind. Unfortunately, the wind was too strong, and the ship's main shaft was suddenly damaged. The situation was dangerous. The captain immediately dropped anchor, but the wind became stronger and stronger, and the anchor lost its support.

Ship's Anchor Drifting

and drifted backward. At this moment, the captain and crew were terrified because they had entered a stage that was beyond their ability to resist. The captain urgently sent an SOS distress call, hoping for assistance from other ships. The Huitong head office in Yantai received the alert first and immediately notified Shanghai. The Shanghai office immediately sent a telegram to the Incheon office, ordering it to inquire about the truth of the accident and to quickly seek rescue measures nearby. It also telegraphed the Shanghai branch. Until yesterday morning, it received

Incheon's Reply

stating that the "Litong" steamship's main shaft had been damaged and that the ship had encountered danger in the strong wind and waves. Even the anchor that had been dropped had drifted with the wind. Now, the ship has reported that the wind has gradually subsided, the ship is safe, and it will not drift aimlessly again. The company was somewhat relieved to receive this telegram, but the details are still unclear and it has telegraphed the ship's captain again to quickly report the details.

Tianjin Artificial Silk Piece Goods: Sales Method; Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Receives Ministry of Finance Instructions 90

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, upon receiving a letter from the Silk and Satin Trade Association, stated that it was inappropriate to issue sales permits without requiring supplementary tax payments for artificial silk piece goods in Tianjin, and that the establishment of a General Inspection Office in Hebei and Chahar would hinder tax revenue. After forwarding the letter to the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Finance replied yesterday, "The submission has been noted. The inspection and clearance methods for piece goods made of artificial silk or mixed with artificial silk have been previously stipulated and implemented by this Ministry, and have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and filing. All artificial silk accumulated by factories that comply with the regulations, cleared, and reported to the Customs should be subject to supplementary tax payments if they cannot provide evidence of tax payment. As for accumulated piece goods, the Customs shall issue sales permits. Factories throughout the country shall handle this uniformly. This Ministry previously received a telegram from the Director-General of Customs, stating that the Tianjin Weaving and Dyeing Industry Association had checked and verified the amount of accumulated artificial silk, piece goods, and silk warp stored on the machines by the factory members. The Tianjin Customs has been ordered to collect supplementary tax payments for the accumulated artificial silk and silk warp stored on the machines, and to issue sales permits for the accumulated piece goods. This is handled according to the original method. After the clearance, the artificial silk used and the piece goods woven by the factories will be subject to thorough inspection by the Customs in accordance with the regulations, which can prevent the malpractice of purchasing smuggled artificial silk as raw materials for piece goods. It can also help maintain the business of legitimate merchants. The request of the Association is not in accordance with the regulations and should not be discussed. Except for the section on the proposed establishment of an inspection office in Hebei and Chahar to inspect goods and collect consumption tax, which will be handled separately, it is appropriate to approve and instruct to be informed. This is the approval."

National Lawyers Association: Standing Committee Meeting Today 96

Zhang Shijie Left for Beijing Last Night

The National Lawyers Association is scheduled to hold its Sixth Standing Committee Meeting of the Seventh Session at its clubhouse on Fengfu Road, Nanjing, at 10 a.m. today (Sunday) to discuss important motions. The Shanghai Wuxian, Hangxian, and other lawyers associations have all nominated representatives to attend. Mr. Zhang Shijie, Secretary-General of the National Lawyers Association, left for Beijing by overnight train last night to participate in the meeting.

North China Daily News Reports: Fessenden Discusses the Authority of the Municipal Council; Maintaining Peace and Order in the Concession Relies on the Decision of the Consular Body 97

The North China Daily News reports that this morning (3rd), a reporter from the North China Daily News interviewed Mr. Fessenden, Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council, and asked about the Municipal Council's attitude towards the extraordinary situation in the Hongkou District in the past few days. Mr. Fessenden replied that the Shanghai Municipal Council is an authority responsible for maintaining law and order within the International Settlement. However, a development of the situation that is beyond the power of the Municipal Council becomes a national diplomatic event and is somewhat beyond the control of the municipal authorities. The Japanese Marines have no legal authority to prohibit the police officers of the Municipal Council from freely acting in the performance of their duties, as has happened in recent days. However, soldiers, whether they belong to Japan or another country, often become overly enthusiastic when performing what they consider to be their duties, especially when it involves the honor of their country. They are easily prone to overstepping their legal rights due to temporary ignorance. Furthermore, the Japanese Marines have no legal authority to detain or confiscate the property of people of non-Japanese nationality within the Settlement, as has happened occasionally in recent times. However, residents of Shanghai overestimate the authority granted by the Municipal Council to the Police Department and forget that the Municipal Council is bound by the Land Regulations. Any extraordinary resolutions must be submitted to the Consular Body for a decision. All countries participating in the Shanghai Municipality have the right to send troops ashore to the Settlement to protect the lives and property of their nationals. The Municipal Council is entrusted by the authorities of various countries to maintain peace and order within the Settlement, but its authority is a municipal authority, and it has no power in itself. When Japanese soldiers landed and took over the management of the Hongkou area, a situation arose that was beyond the power of the Municipal Council. This must be arbitrated through diplomatic channels by the officials of the countries involved. The Japanese soldiers' seizure of police power to detain prisoners was completely wrong. However, the Municipal Council has no power or legal provisions to deal with this extremely complex point, so this matter will still be resolved through diplomatic negotiations. The Municipal Council has absolutely no authority to interfere with foreign troops stationed in Shanghai because the Municipal Council does not have the power of a sovereign state. If the situation reaches a critical point, the Municipal Council must refer it to the Consular Body for a decision.

Yesterday's Pujiang River: Sudden High Tide, Exceeding Forecast, Ankle-Deep Flooding on Low Roads 98

Yesterday was the 18th day of the eighth lunar month, a major tide season, so the tide in the Pujiang River was quite high, close to the revetment. Low-lying roads were flooded, requiring vehicles for ferrying. The situation at the time is recorded below:

Tide Reaches Riverbank

Yesterday at 1:59 PM, the high tide in the Pujiang River exceeded the prediction of the Huangpu River Dredging Bureau (predicted height: 11 feet 1 inch). It was less than half a foot from the Bund revetment. The tide, agitated by the ship propellers, inundated low-lying areas such as the Bund Park and the Shiliupu Bund, creating a vast expanse of water, a spectacular sight. The boats along the shore appeared as if they were about to be rowed ashore, a truly unusual scene.

Roads Flooded

Many low-lying roads were flooded by the high tide. For example, in front of the Outer Customs House, water reached the stone steps. The section of Second Road from Sichuan Road in the west to the Bund in the east, as well as the intersection of Fifth Road and Sichuan Road, were ankle-deep in water. Water accumulated into a channel from the China General Edison Company on Sichuan Road to the side of the East Asia Bank. Pedestrians had to use rickshaws for ferrying. Several inches of water also accumulated in front of the Shanghai Municipal Council on Fourth Road and in front of Wing On Company on Nanjing Road.

Four Counties on High Alert

Today is the peak of the high tide. The Jiangnan seawalls in the four counties of Baoshan, Taicang, Songjiang, and Changshu should be carefully protected to avoid danger. The Jiangnan Water Conservancy Bureau has specifically instructed the counties to pay close attention to ensure the safety of the lives and property of the people in these four counties.

Two Corpses Case at Hongkou Women's Hospital: Court Hears Murder Details, Buying Diploma and Committing Murder, Concubine Admits Helping at the Scene, Judge Carefully Orders Further Interrogation 100

The widely publicized case of the buried male and female corpses at Hongkou Women's Hospital involved the main male perpetrator, Zhang Wenhua (27 years old, Shanghainese, also known by ten other aliases, including Gu Penggan), and the main female perpetrator, Zhang's concubine Chen Xiaobao (also known as Liang Meiyu and Xu Shuzhen, 25 years old, Shanghainese). They were arrested by Chinese Detective Zhou Guisen, Detective Inspector Cui Chengke, Huang Fugen, Xu Decheng, and Detectives Shen Binkui, Qiu Zhenting, Wang Dongchen of the Hongkou Concession Police, along with detectives from the French Concession Police, at 9:00 AM the day before yesterday in the attic room at No. 13, Lane 455, Kangding Road. Over 900 yuan in banknotes was seized. They were taken back to the police station and detained separately.

Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court and charged with murder under Article 271 of the Criminal Code. Many men and women were in the audience. The details of the trial are recorded below. First, Judge Zhong Qing inquired about the age, place of origin, occupation, and address of Zhang Wenhua and Chen Xiaobao. Then, the police lawyer Zhang Shizhu stood up and described the case's breakthrough: "On September 4th of this year, Yu Gengsheng, a man, and Lu Aili, a woman, were strangled to death at Hongkou Women's Hospital. The circumstances of the discovery of their bodies were detailed in previous statements when the two defendants' hired maid, Fei Wang, and driver, Chen Pengfei, were requested for detention. As this matter was of great importance, the police immediately

conducted a careful investigation and learned that Chen Xiaobao's sister, Chen Abao, was residing at No. 25, Lane 95, Avenue Petain in the French Concession. We went to investigate and learned that Chen Abao was indeed living with her sister, but they had recently moved to No. 63, Rue Jules Pestel. The detectives went to No. 63 to investigate, but discovered that they had moved elsewhere on September 15th. It was also found that the moving was entrusted to the Tong'an Moving Company at No. 9, Lane 104, Avenue Haig. The detectives learned from Tong'an Company that the defendants had moved to No. 13, Lane 215, Kangding Road. The detectives went to No. 13 and were informed by the tenant Zhu Ahui that the defendants had moved to No. 13, Lane 455 on the same road on September 29th. Therefore, the two

defendants were arrested there early the day before yesterday. It was also learned that Zhang Wenhua's wife, Zhang Yao, was also living with them, but she had moved to the home of a relative, Lu Yunliang, at No. 6, Jia 10, Bao 8, Xiaoyingfang, Chuansha, Pudong before the arrest. The detectives, together with Chen Liande, the chief of the local Public Security Bureau, went to arrest Zhang Yao, but were unsuccessful. Zhang Wenhua graduated from the MacMillan Academy in 1928 and then worked as a nurse at Baolong Hospital for three years, but did not complete his term. In 1931, he transferred to another hospital and, for 200 yuan,

obtained the abortion business on Broadway. On September 2nd of this year, Yu Gengsheng from Sichuan, accompanied by Lu Aili, went to Hongkou Women's Hospital for an abortion, stating that the surgery fee was 35 yuan. That evening, the defendants first examined Lu. The surgery began at 8:00 AM the next morning. Due to the surgeon's lack of skill, Lu's uterus was punctured, causing severe bleeding and a dangerous situation. Yu Gengsheng, who accompanied her,

argued strongly with the defendants, leading them to have murderous intentions. On September 4th, Yu was injected with an anesthetic needle. As Yu was dying, he was strangled with a towel to death. Lu was also given an anesthetic injection, and Liang Meiyu stuffed gauze into her mouth, suffocating her to death. The two bodies were then buried underground. Liang bought 150 pounds of lime from Taiji Lime Store at No. 89, Xinjiabang Road, and lead sheets from Huiyuanxiang Hardware Store at No. 203, Tangshan Road. Zhang and Hua borrowed tools from Chen Linji Carpenter Shop at No. 314, Zhaofeng Road, to

pry open the floorboards and bury the two bodies. On September 7th, the defendants, along with Zhang's wife and Liang's sister, hired a Chinese Moving Company to move their belongings to No. 6, Lane 311, Rue Montigny, and No. 8, Dahua Lane, Nanyang Bridge, and frequently returned to Hongkou Women's Hospital to listen for news until they moved to Rue Jules Pestel on September 15th, after which they stopped checking the news. The police have now exhumed the bodies from under the Hongkou Women's Hospital, photographed them, and presented them as evidence." Zhang Wenhua confessed that he had worked as a nurse at Baolong Hospital but had not completed his apprenticeship before working at another hospital. Chen Xiaobao was his concubine. On April 1st of last year, they opened Hongkou Women's Hospital, specializing in treating women's dysmenorrhea, anemia, and tuberculosis. On September 2nd, Yu Gengsheng from Sichuan and Lu Aili came to the hospital for an abortion, stating that the fee was 35 yuan. As usual, I would first examine Lu's lower body and

perform the surgery, but in the past, I had never made a mistake when performing abortions. This time, it was because I was

having trouble with something, and I used too much force when starting, causing her uterus to rupture and her abdomen to gradually swell, leading to a very dangerous situation. At 2:00 AM on September 4th, Yu Gengsheng rang the bell downstairs. I went downstairs and saw the woman's eyes were white and she was barely breathing. Yu argued strongly with me and refused to give up. I then had murderous intentions and wanted to die with Yu so I could silence him. I lied to Yu, saying that the only way to save the woman was to borrow his blood. Yu agreed. We went upstairs together, and I killed him with a German anesthetic needle. It was just a misunderstanding, but when Judge Zhong asked Zhang during the autopsy, "There was still gauze around Yu's neck. Why was that?" Zhang replied, "Although the person was dead, I was afraid he would come back to life

as a zombie, so I wrapped gauze around his neck to cut off his breath. The cloth in Lu's mouth was because her stomach had rotted, to prevent the odor from coming out, and I was afraid she would come back to life, so I gave her another injection. Afterwards, I borrowed iron tools from a nearby carpenter shop to bury the bodies underground." Chen Xiaobao confessed that she had an affair with Zhang and that they had met because Zhang had rented her extra house. Later, Zhang opened a hospital and invited her to be a nurse, and they lived together. On September 2nd, a man and a woman came for an abortion. After the diagnosis, it was determined that the woman was three months pregnant. When asked why she wanted an abortion, the woman replied that there were various reasons why she had to have one. I initially asked for a surgery fee of 40 yuan, but we agreed on 35 yuan. Zhang performed the abortion, and I only

helped from the side. The rest of my testimony is the same as Zhang's, to be brief. In the end, she said that we were both young and inexperienced, and that Zhang Wenhua had an elderly father at home, and asked for leniency. Zhang and Chen both hired lawyers Fan Gang and Yu Siliang to defend them. Judge Zhong said that the case still required investigation, so he ordered the defendants to be detained for further interrogation on the 13th, and also ordered the lime shop, hardware store, and carpenter shop witnesses to be summoned for questioning.

Japanese Sailor Tagang Killed: Zhang Ronghe Interrogated Yesterday; Police Believe Zhang Is a Major Suspect, But Zhang Denies Any Knowledge of the Matter 101

At 8:20 PM on the 23rd of last month, a Japanese sailor named Tagang Asao was shot and killed at the intersection of Haining Road and Wusong Road, in front of the Shanghai Bank, a Japanese business. At the same time, two other Japanese sailors who were with Tagang, Yahata Yoshiharu and Izuto Yozo, were also injured. Another sailor escaped unscathed. After the incident, the Japanese Marines stationed in Shanghai were immediately dispatched to the area near the scene and arrested three suspects: Zhang Ronghe, a Tai Zhou street vendor, Ma Yongcai, a worker from the Hongxing Printing House from Jiading and Ma Yongnian. A pistol was found in a sand box at the entrance of Lane 15, Haining Road, and another pistol was found in Yuqingfang, Haining Road. Afterwards, the Public Concession Police handed Zhang and the other two over to the First Special District Court with the approval of the Japanese Command, requesting their detention. These facts have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the case was continued. Ma Yongcai and Ma Yongnian hired lawyer Ping Heng to appear in court. Subsequently, Judge Zhong Qing of the First Special District Court opened the Third Criminal Court for interrogation. The police lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that after investigation, the police found insufficient evidence against the suspects Ma Yongcai and Ma Yongnian, and they were mistakenly arrested while passing by. Therefore, it was decided not to prosecute them, and the court was requested to stop their detention and release them. Zhang Ronghe was considered a major suspect, so a postponement of one week was requested. The gun found in the sand box in Lane 15, as well as the nine shell casings and one bullet found, were all tested by the firearms department and confirmed to have been fired from that gun. The gun found in Yuqingfang was tested and found not to have been used. At this point, Judge Zhong ordered the release of Ma Yongcai and Ma Yongnian, and the police took the two away. Only Zhang Ronghe remained. Lawyer Zhang Shizhu continued to state that there were as many as 25 witnesses in Zhang Ronghe's case, and they had all made statements at the police station. However, only three Japanese witnesses were present in court today: Horiue Tadashi, Suehiro Akio, and Miyata Hajime. According to Hori's statement to the police, he was a tailor living at No. 114, Lane 332, Teeswell Road. On the day of the incident, he was at a meeting at No. 6, Lane 15, Haining Road when he suddenly heard gunshots. He rushed out, initially suspecting that the gunshots came from North Haining Road, so he went there but saw nothing unusual. Then he circled around Wusong Road to South Haining Road and saw a crowd gathered at the entrance of Lane 15 (the lane connects South Haining Road and North Haining Road at both ends). He saw two old women kneeling on the ground, and Zhang Ronghe was opening the lid of the sand box with his left hand, opening it about six inches, and then putting something black in his right hand into the box. At that time, Hori said to Zhang, "You killed the person!" Zhang immediately closed the lid of the box. Hori stepped forward and arrested Zhang, and a gun was found in the box. Suehiro and Miyata's testimonies were the same. According to Suehiro, he was working in the wireless business at No. 519, Haining Road. He heard gunshots and went out to see three Japanese soldiers lying on the ground on Wusong Road, seemingly seriously injured. Then he met an uninjured Japanese soldier in a Japanese bookstore (translated as Xue Shan Du), who told him the location of the incident. He rushed over and saw Zhang standing about a yard away from the sand box, and he helped Horiue Tadashi arrest him. He also presented a map. Horiue Tadashi also submitted a statement to prove everything, and his statement was the same as the lawyer Zhang's statement. (Omitted) When Zhang Ronghe was interrogated, he confessed that he was indeed arrested by Horiue Tadashi, three or four steps away from the sand box. Because he heard gunshots at the time, he suspected that his fellow countryman Chang Tai was harmed (Chang Tai also set up a congee stall near Lane 15), so he went to investigate and was arrested. Chang Tai lives at No. 92, Dongxing Lane, Teeswell Road. He did not kill the Japanese soldiers and did not know who killed them. The police lawyer Zhang stood up and said that Chang Tai was indeed a person who set up a congee stall near the scene. He also made a statement at the police station. Zhang Ronghe and his mother did set up a congee stall about 67 yards west of Lane 15. He also presented a map. Judge Zhong Qing interrogated Suehiro Akio about his experience in helping Horiue Tadashi. Miyata Hajime's statement was the same as Suehiro's, so he was not questioned in detail. It was announced that the matter would be adjourned until 2:00 PM on the 9th of this month for further interrogation.

Shanghai Municipal Council Actively Streamlining: Dissolving Volunteer Corps Artillery Units 105

Board Meeting Minutes Record Merits; Hope Soldiers Do Not Disperse.

For the sake of active streamlining, the Shanghai Municipal Council recently approved the recommendation of the Defence Committee at a board meeting to dissolve the existing two artillery units of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps. This proposal was decided by the Defence Committee on September 21st, after considering reports from all relevant departments, and recommended to the Board that it be terminated immediately. The reasons for the termination are two-fold. First, after the dissolution of the artillery unit, direct recurring costs can be saved by 15,000 yuan per year, and the vacated buildings can be used for the urgently needed expansion of the General Office and the Rates Office. Furthermore, the Shanghai Volunteer Corps' current light artillery is outdated, and the ammunition is nearing its expiration date. If it is not dissolved, the purchase of new ammunition would require a huge sum of money, which is beyond the current financial capacity. In addition, there is no suitable location for exercises other than Hong Kong, and the travel expenses would be difficult to arrange. Second, in terms of practicality, the artillery unit must have rigorous training to achieve superior effectiveness, and both personnel and equipment must be constantly improved. The Shanghai Volunteer Corps' scope of activity is limited to Shanghai, so it is felt that the artillery unit is too much for a volunteer corps to handle. It is heard that the commander of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps has agreed to the termination of the artillery unit but expressed that the excellent members of the two artillery units should not be allowed to disperse after this. He hopes that they will understand the necessity of the termination and join other teams or special police to serve the community. Furthermore, the community as a whole should have a considerable sense of gratitude for the past service of the artillery unit. General Macnaghten spoke next, saying that although he had agreed to the dissolution, he had once been the commanding officer of the unit, so he felt regret at the demise of the unit. He hoped that all parties would have a correct understanding of this matter, and that the excellent members of the unit would not be allowed to disperse afterward. He also said that the Board of Directors of the Municipal Council should express gratitude for the unit's past excellent performance. The Chairman then moved that the Board unanimously record its gratitude for the past service of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Artillery Unit and hoped that the officers and soldiers of the unit would not be allowed to disperse in the future.

The Jingjiang Bandit Wu Zhenrong Was Hanged Yesterday: Original Name Chen Mingsheng Wrote a Will in Court, Asked for a Full Meal Before Death and Sang Peking Opera: A Person Who Disregarded the Law Has Been Hanged According to the Law 107

The bandit Wu Zhenrong (29 years old), also known as Chen Mingsheng, from Jingjiang, was sentenced to death for leading accomplices to rob the Jixing Pawnshop at No. 640 Haining Road at 9:55 PM on July 28th of last year and killing Chaozhou native Wang Xiangxun when the robbery failed. After the case was discovered, he was arrested by Chinese and foreign detectives from the Hongkou Concession Police and brought to the First Special District Court for questioning. The Jiangsu Provincial Government approved the death sentence the day before yesterday and ordered its execution. He was sent to the Third Criminal Court yesterday morning. Judge Shen Shanzeng presided over the court and asked him if he had any last words and if he wanted to write to his family. He said that his father and wife had died many years ago, and his old home was in Sidunzi, Jingjiang, with only a few houses, which were managed by his brother. He planned to entrust his paternal uncle, Ming Xueyou, to sell the property and have his cousin Wenlin come to Shanghai to collect his body. The court had him write a letter in his own hand, which he did briefly: "(To my dear uncle, I hope you are well. Your nephew did not listen to your teachings and has come to this. I did not listen to my uncle Xueyou's words in the past because I was doing bad things outside. I am now being executed on the 18th day of the eighth lunar month. I am having my cousin Wenlin collect my body. The land and property at home should be sold, and there must be no mistakes. Your nephew Chen Mingsheng, sent to Chen Xueyou at Yongfeng Pharmacy, Sidunzi, Jingjiang)." He was calm and said that he had not had a full meal in prison (execution prisoners are given two yuan for meals, and the police were ordered to buy him food) so that he could be a full ghost. Judge Shen ordered Wu Zhenrong to be sent to the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate for execution by hanging, and the Chinese and foreign police of the police station took him away, along with the case file, and handed him over to the Shanghai Local Court for execution, appointing Prosecutor Xie Lian as the supervising officer. The prosecutor immediately led the clerk Zheng Jiyu and Inspector Xuan Zhiming, and also supervised the chief and deputy judicial police officers Zhang Shuping and Chen Xihui, leading execution policemen Shen Tingfang and Zhou Qiwen to the second prison execution ground in Caohejing. The judge, together with Warden Ding Lei, took his seat to begin the case and brought the criminal Wu Zhenrong to the case to confess. "I am not called Wu Zhenrong. My original name is Chen Mingsheng. My cousin is coming to collect my body. Today I die, I am not sad, I am very happy, but my last request is to eat some fruit." The judge smiled and nodded, and ordered him to be taken down for execution. The criminal then sang his Peking opera, a kind of fearless attitude that was very rare. Police Chief Zhang and others directed the bailiffs to tie the criminal to a wooden stake, and the noose was tightened around his neck as required. It took half an hour for him to be strangled to death. The noose was immediately sealed, and the body was left exposed overnight. It was re-examined the next day before being collected for burial.

Fang Baizhou and Wu Guangen: Recommended a Business, Causing a Death - Borrowed Money to Buy a Foot Knife, Lodged to Assassinate, Startled from a Dream, Pursued to Death 108

Fang Baizhou, a 24-year-old from Nanhui, worked as a noodle maker at the Wuweizhai noodle shop at No. 9 Minzhi Ni Yin Road (behind the Gonghe Hall of the Great World) in the French Concession. He had been making noodles for four years. The noodle-making area was set up in the stove room at No. 11 Xin Shou An Li across the street. He also lodged in the noodle-making area at night. When needed, he invited his fellow villager, Wu Guangen (25 years old), to be his substitute. Recently, a certain accountant of Wuweizhai opened a new shop in Xin Zha. Wu asked Fang to recommend business to him. They reached an agreement on August 4th of the lunar calendar (September 19th). On August 10th (September 25th), Wu came to Shanghai from his village, intending to have Fang accompany him to take over the shop. Unexpectedly, someone else had already taken it over, and Wu's chance for business fell through. Fang then explained to Wu and told him to return to his village for the time being and wait for him to find another recommendation and notify him to come to Shanghai to take over the shop. Who knew that Wu would misunderstand and think that Fang was unwilling to recommend him and was meddling, so he had the idea of suspecting and killing Fang to vent his anger. On the afternoon of the 2nd, he went to Fang's place, falsely claiming that he was sick and had no money to buy medicine, and borrowed five jiao of silver from Fang. Fang lent him the money as requested. Wu got the money and went to Ximen to buy a foot knife about an inch wide and four inches long, hiding it on his person. In the evening, he went to Fang's place again to borrow a place to stay. Fang did not suspect anything and readily agreed, inviting him to sleep over. Wu slept until about 5 a.m. yesterday morning. Taking advantage of Fang's deep sleep, he took out the hidden foot knife and stabbed Fang in the right side of his throat. Before he could pull the knife out, he turned and ran out of the door into the alley. Fang, startled awake by the pain in his dream, jumped up to chase the murderer. Fang was shirtless and barefoot, wearing only short trousers, and his body was covered in blood. He chased him to the intersection of Minzhi Ni Yin Road and Avenue Edward VII. Fang pulled the foot knife out of his neck, and fresh blood gushed out like a tide. His body collapsed to the ground due to extreme pain. At that time, Hong Chenfu (37-year-old Anhui native), the gatekeeper of No. 722 Xin Shou An Li, caught a glimpse of it, helped catch up, and apprehended the murderer Wu Guangen. They called the police and brought him into the Avenue Joffre Police Station. On one hand, they sent detectives to take the injured Fang Baizhou to Renji Hospital by car. Because the wound bled too much, he died at 5:30 without medical treatment. The hospital notified the French Police Station, who transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Sub-Hall for an autopsy. At 10 a.m., the police sent the criminal to the Second Special District Court. Court President Wang Gangxu of the Criminal Court came to the First Criminal Court to interrogate him. The lawyer of the Police Department said that the defendant was arrested this morning for murder. The Police Department has not yet investigated the case, and requested that the defendant be detained to investigate the facts of the case and change the date to file a lawsuit for trial. Then, Detective Ma Yizhi reported the process of arresting the defendant and presented the murder weapon. When asked, the defendant Wu Guangen confessed that on the 4th, he asked the deceased to recommend business, and he agreed to recommend him. After he got the recommendation, he came to Shanghai on the 10th to take over the shop. He said that the business had been taken by someone else, so he was angry. Yesterday afternoon, he went to Ximen to buy a knife, stayed at his place that night, and when he was fast asleep at dawn, he stabbed him once and ran away. There was no other resentment, and so on. After verifying the confession in court, it was ordered that the trial be rescheduled for the morning of the 9th. The defendant was taken back into custody. At noon, Judge Wang Ren of the Second Special District Court, accompanied by medical examiner Jiang and Clerk Peng, etc., came to the hall to examine the body. The criminal was brought by the detectives, and his confession was the same as before. The official questioned the witnesses Hong Chenfu and Zhang Yusheng, etc. Because the deceased's family was still in the countryside, the official ordered that it be verified that Fang Baizhou died of knife wounds, and the body was handed over to Tongren Fuyuan Hall for burial. The defendant will be sent to the court for trial. It is heard that the deceased has not yet started a family, and there are an elderly mother and younger brother in his hometown. His shop owner has sent someone to his hometown to urge them to come to Shanghai to collect the body.

Xuan Sheng Case Under Investigation - Involving Visitors 109

Zhang Yongfu Visited on Bail - Miss Chen Er Does Not Recognize Him

The case of the Japanese businessman Xuan Sheng being assassinated on Avenue Disweili and Qimei Road has recently been solved by the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, who arrested the criminals Wang Zhensheng, Mao Yonghu, Zhao Yunhong, Jin Daohong, and women Wang Zai Shi and Zhang Mo Shi, etc. All six of them confessed that they were instigated by the reactionary cadre Hua Ke to assassinate Xuan Sheng in order to cause international disputes. A pistol was confiscated and a document was moved to the local court for investigation. However, the person in charge of this case is Prosecutor Xie Lian. Because he wanted to use investigative tactics to further recruit accomplices, he notified the detention center that if anyone came to visit the above-mentioned male and female criminals, they should detain the visitor for interrogation. The day before yesterday, a man from Qingjiang named Zhang Yongfu, 48 years old, residing at No. 75 Baxiang Bridge, Dadongmen, went to the detention center to visit Zhang Mo Shi, claiming that Zhang Mo Shi was his cousin. The detention center reported this to the prosecutor, who detained Zhang Yongfu and opened a court to interrogate him. Zhang confessed that he used to be a cook on a ship in Luoyang and now sells ducks and chickens. His cousin Zhang Mo Shi lives nearby at No. 72 Shachang Street. Because Mao Yonghu in this case was arrested at Zhang Mo Shi's house, she was also implicated and detained, so he came to visit her. The judge believed that Zhang Yongfu was not suspected of anything, but he still had to be released on bail and prove that he was a good person. He then asked Zhang if he had any relatives or friends in Shanghai who could vouch for him. Zhang said that there was a Miss Chen Er who works as a female guard at Jiangsu Second Prison in Caohejing, who could vouch for him. Yesterday, Prosecutor Xie, taking advantage of the execution of death row inmate Wu Zhenrong by the First Special District Court, brought Zhang to the prison to meet with Prison Director Ding Lei and summoned Miss Chen Er to the court for questioning. However, as soon as Zhang saw Miss Chen Er, he shouted at her. Unexpectedly, Miss Chen Er looked blank and said that she did not recognize him. Even after Zhang's repeated requests and the judge's explanation, Miss Chen Er could not vouch for him. Therefore, he had to be taken back into custody and find another guarantor.

Filmmaker Ma Loufang: Doting on a Concubine and Abandoning His Wife 110

Bai Suzhen Bitterly Accuses Him of Being Deceived - Wei Dixing is Unavoidably Guilty of Adultery

Ma Loufen, a film star, director, and director of the Miaoyin Dance Troupe from Suzhou, 27 years old this year, married Bai Suzhen (21 years old this year), a woman from Beiping, four years ago. They lived with his parents at No. 16 Xingshun Nan Li, Remi Road, in the French Concession. The couple's love was very deep, and they had a daughter named Die Nan, who is two years old this year. Last month of this year, when Ma led the troupe members to perform in Nanyang, he had a relationship with Wei Dixing, a female troupe member from Hangzhou, 19 years old this year. After returning to China, he kept Wei at home in the name of teacher and student. Later, because his wife was by his side, it was inconvenient for him to act. He rented a room on the second floor of a Russian house at No. 226 Ladu Road and lived with Wei. From then on, he did not return home to stay overnight, ignored his wife Bai, and did not care about his wife's life. Recently, Bai found the residence of Ma and Wei and reported to the French Police Station on the 2nd through Lawyer Bian Lu. Lawyer Yuan Jiahuan of the Police Department stated the case and filed a public prosecution for the crime of disrupting the family according to Article 239 of the Criminal Law. The court believed that the case was related to public morals and should be prohibited from onlookers. The defendants admitted to adultery during the trial. The court announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the 7th. The defendants were each released on bail of 500 yuan. After the defendants requested a reduction, the court approved it and each reduced the bail to 300 yuan. Without bail, they were taken into custody. According to Ma's wife Bai, when Ma returned from Nanyang, he brought Wei home, saying that Wei's parents were not in Shanghai and that she was temporarily borrowing a place to stay. They were just teacher and student, and she did not suspect anything else. At night, Ma slept on the bed, and she and Wei slept on the floor. Until recently, when her parents-in-law celebrated their birthday, Wei paid respects to her parents-in-law, and her parents-in-law called Wei "new grandmother" and her younger uncle called Wei "sister-in-law." She did not understand the reason and questioned Ma. He admitted that he had newly married her as a concubine, and her parents-in-law also wanted her to admit it. She refused and opposed it. Ma then went out with Wei to rent a house and live together. When she was at home, her parents-in-law abused her. Ma did not return home from August 1st. When she was at home, she worked every day and was more bitter than a maid. Unable to bear it, she found out the residence of Ma and others and reported it to the police station for arrest.

Training Relief Teams 117

The China Southeast Joint Office of the World Red Swastika Society, in view of the fact that there are many difficulties and frequent disasters in the world, and that relief talents are often insufficient, specially established the General Supervisory Office for Relief Team Training in Shanghai this year. Zhou Zongliang was publicly elected as the general supervisor, and Wu Zhongyan, Ling Youzeng, Huang Bicen, and Li Dianchen were the deputy supervisors. Luo Buzhou was the training director and was responsible for training relief talents in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Fujian provinces. Jiangsu Province is divided into five districts (Jiangbei) (Songhu) (Changtai (Xuhai) (Jingzhen Dan), Zhejiang Province is one district, Anhui Province is divided into two districts (North Anhui) (Central and Southern Anhui), and Fujian Province is one district, for a total of nine districts. The trainees in Songhu are recommended by each district, and the graduation period is six months. The Jiangbei and Changtai districts are trained in Changzhou, and the Jingzhen district is trained in the capital. Two districts in North Anhui and Central and Southern Anhui each form a training team, and Fujian Province is trained by the Fuzhou branch. There are more than 100 students in total. Currently, the graduates include the Songhu, Zhejiang, Jiangbei, Changtai, Jingzhen, North Anhui, and Central and Southern Anhui districts. There is also the ordinary school of Juegang in Wuwu, Anhui, which is currently under training. In addition, the Wuhan district is training a class of more than 20 people. It is heard that the training course of the association includes rescue, medicine, transportation, and burial. Attention is paid to anti-virus, first aid, and stretcher methods. It also teaches wartime knowledge and wartime international law. All graduates have been assigned to various associations for internships. The General Training Office has organized seven major joint relief teams. Each team can be divided into two or three squadrons, stationed in Shanghai, Jiangsu, Beijing, Zhenjiang, Changzhou, Taiyuan, Xuhai, Ningbo in Zhejiang, Hangzhou, Wuhu in Anhui, Bengbu, Fuzhou in Fujian, and other places, in order to handle relief work at any time in case of disaster. Chen Fuyin, Hu Zhongcheng, Ling Yuanlang, Liu Huigen, Chen Tianru, Chen Wangqiu, Liu Xiangdao, and others were publicly elected as the team supervisors.

Chinese Institute of Engineers - Acting to Recruit Factory Managers 121

The Chinese Institute of Engineers has announced that a certain factory intends to recruit factory managers. Anyone who is healthy, of high moral character, and male, with a high school or vocational school diploma, has worked for more than four years and has chemical and mechanical knowledge, or has graduated from a university or specialized school in mechanical engineering or applied chemistry, can take the exam. During the practice and probation period, a stipend of 30 yuan will be issued.
