Scenery of Greater Shanghai

Miniature Model of the Officialdom Scene a Century Ago 181

— Qian Fengshi

"Shanghai has everything," no one can deny this saying. Recently, there is another fascinating place that makes everyone who sees it marvel, that is the "Family Miniature Model" on display on the fourth floor of the Great Sun Department Store. There is a full set of old-fashioned dowry, old-fashioned wedding hall and bridal chamber arrangement; a full set of civil and military official escorts for the old-fashioned grand funeral; the style of the ancestral hall; old-fashioned longevity hall, banquet hall, flower hall; temporary stage; a pleasure boat for lake tours; a Suzhou-style kitchen; and various application furniture. Even the Suzhou-style food peddlers shouting along the street and their respective utensils are all available, complete in every detail. This model vividly brings the old antiques of the old-fashioned patriarchal society of a century ago into the eyes of us Shanghai people who are full of Europeanization, making us naturally think of the past situation of the official families of the late Qing Dynasty, and we can't help but feel the feeling of where are they now.

This is a retired Qing Dynasty military officer named Zhou, who has lived in Suzhou for a long time. According to the title of his small honor guard, this gentleman is called Shaofu, and his name is Zhou Dunhoutang. This gentleman has no special hobbies in his life, and almost devotes his entire energy to this "small thing". Don't look at these small models; the materials used are: copper, iron, glass, wood, silk, porcelain, leather, paper, ... No matter what the material, it must be prepared, customized, fired, mounted, and sewn according to the real thing. It is comparable to imitating the porcelain of Jingdezhen, the paper of Xuanzhou, the silk of Huzhou, ... etc. No matter the value, it must be made locally. Therefore, the price of these small toys is often dozens or hundreds of times that of the real big toys? Moreover, that kind of unreserved, uncompromising realism is even more exhaustive!

Entering the door of the exhibition hall, we first see a painted boat. Anyone who has been to Suzhou and Wuxi will immediately think of its popular name called "Wuxi Kuai". At the same time, they will also think of the scene of "singing and dancing boats, hairpin shadows wave first" in the previous prosperous times? Although this boat is a prototype, it is eight or nine feet long. The whole body is made of real tung oil and high-quality wood. It is divided into five cabins. The first cabin at the bow is arranged as an open hall, except for the deck at the entrance. The entrance to the cabin is decorated with five-color glass (it seems to be glazed tiles), and the sides are equipped with water pavilion-style screen doors with flower boards and glass windows. In front of it are arranged four sets of master chairs and tea tables. The top is a bright tile ceiling, and under it are hung many hexagonal rectangular high-legged gauze lanterns, and colorful balls are tied. A lamp in the center is like a Western-style safety kerosene lamp, hanging lower. In the open hall, there is a table for eight immortals, with chairs and tables, and a set of mahjong tiles. The mahjong tiles are small, but they are all made of real ivory and bamboo backs, with dice and zhuangzi complete. The covered teacups and water pipes are also fully equipped on the table. In the middle cabin, separated by a large glass screen door, the layout is slightly the same as the open hall, but this cabin is a dining room, with a round table in the center. The table is equipped with hot pot bowls, basins, hand dishes, chopsticks, and spoons. The tables and chairs are also brightly painted. Entering the inner part of the dining room through the screen door, it is a place for lying down and traveling, equipped with a pit table, pit cushions, large spittoons, foot pedals, etc., which are arranged in the usual way, without any omissions. In addition to the straw mat, there is also a terrace on the roof of the middle and rear cabins, which is prepared for tourists to climb up and take a look. Its shape is like a sun deck, but it is very elegant, and the four pillars are hung with bright lights. In the rear cabin, the items used by the boatmen are also fully equipped. The mast, rudder, oar, paddle, pole, anchor, etc. in the boat are all like the real thing. If it is placed in the middle of the river, it will definitely move freely and be gorgeous and pleasing to the eye.

Picture 1 182

— (Photographed by Yu Luli)

The wedding hall (see Figure 1) is three feet high and four feet long, and the lower part is an open hall with three large bays in front and back, which is a miniature of the hall of an old-fashioned official family. The upper floor is divided into three rooms. The middle is the ancestral hall, the left is the bridal chamber, and the right is the companion's bedroom and the place where the bride's boxes are placed together. In addition to two large jujube red lacquered quilt boxes, there are also twelve large and small vermilion lacquered clothing boxes, etc., which are arranged in the room according to the law. The bright and gorgeous arrangement of the bridal chamber is so dazzling that, in short, it has all the beauty and is not lacking in splendor. The full set of dowry is placed in the wedding hall downstairs. All the old-fashioned vermilion lacquered gaily boxes are displayed in dozens of frames. The silk and satin, clothes, shoes, and socks are all colorful and magnificent. What is especially interesting is the vermilion lacquer so-called descendants bucket - the toilet, which is completely in accordance with the custom, with dozens of large and small ones, and all of them are edged with high-grade red lacquer and gold.

The size of the longevity hall is slightly like the wedding hall, and the furniture is completely made of mahogany. But there is no building. Longevity banners and couplets are hung all over it, with lanterns and colors, and gold characters compete with red candles, reflecting each other, and there is indeed a feeling of longevity for the eyes and a hall full of gold and jade. Although the equipment in the back hall is relatively simple, there are dining tables, pit beds, and account tables. The four treasures of the study and abacus are arranged in a small row, which is very interesting. In front of the longevity hall is an ancestral hall gatehouse. It is slightly like a temple gate, but there are no clay sculptures. However, the four walls of the gatehouse are surrounded by countless plaques, all of which are in pairs on the left and right. Such as hereditary Hanlin Academy, Doctor of Jingjing, Wugong General, rewarded with peacock feathers...etc. Beside the ancestral hall, there is also a water pavilion, a cool pavilion, and a flower hall. Next to it is a Suzhou-style official kitchen (see Figure), which is divided into three questions. Two-thirds of the area is the kitchen. The northernmost big stove has a large pot and soup. In addition to the stove, the dishes, bowls, cupboards and various kitchen utensils, firewood, rice, oil and salt, seven things, are arranged neatly in different positions. The other third of the place is a room where the father and the servant eat; a question from the servant's bedroom, on which there is a small loft. The things used by the servants. The sundries are very detailed. Corresponding to the same place is a collection of peddler's loads. Compared with the rich people's supplies mentioned earlier, they are all detailed, and the peddler's supplies are completely rough goods. All the burdens of selling fried white fruits, selling rice wine, wontons, soup balls, baked sweet potatoes, etc., are all equipped with shoulder poles and rain gear. In addition, there is also a century-old open-air stage, which is a public entertainment temple fair style. The entrance of the stage is full of name plates of famous actors a century ago, and there are two cloth-tied people on the stage, one is in the shape of the Monkey King, and the other is in the shape of a golden-faced monster playing steel, who is originally playing Da Jinqian Leopard.

Picture 2 183

— (Photographed by Yu Luli)

The most distinctive feature is the grand funeral honor guard. In total, there are more than 200 items, such as door guns, flags, paired plaques, inscriptions, Danqi pavilions, etc., including 20 kinds of pavilions, 4 or 5 kinds of umbrellas, 3 or 4 kinds of sedan chairs, as well as eighteen kinds of weapons, various funeral banners, gongs and drums, musical instruments, etc., all of which are about ten times smaller than the real ones, and the length has been extended to four feet. Finally, there is the mourning hall, with the spiritual seat in the middle, and dozens of elegiac couplets hanging beside it. In fact, these are all jokes made by this old gentleman Shaofu, so someone gave the horizontal plaque of the mourning hall the four characters "Dream Awakening Huang Liang". There are two elegiac couplets that say it well. One says: "It is small, the real honor guard is really worth seeing; it is a play, it is a joke, a fake funeral is a fake sadness." The second says: "This world must know that everything is a dream, who does not see it as such?" After reading these two couplets, everyone will probably say that they are just right?

La Bruyere's Quotations 184

— Lin

Whether your future is dark or bright, laugh once first, otherwise, I'm afraid you won't have the chance to laugh before you die.

There are many things in the world that really make you dizzy and forget to eat and sleep before you get them; but after you get them, you feel bored and more boring than you hoped! ——This can be tasted a little from the desire to be a "great man".

Life is short and boring if it is always going on in "hoping for the future"; because of this, all ideals and happiness are placed on the unknowable "future", and by that time, the previous ideals and happiness have disappeared, because one's health and youth have long been different from the past. At this time, we hope for the front again, but the front is still not the place we want to go... So we always hope, always disappoint, and life becomes a tiring outline.

Some people say that the reason why people all over the world cannot form a country, cannot speak the same language, cannot abide by one law, and cannot have the same culture and habits is that they have fundamental differences in spirit, hobbies, and emotions. But I am very surprised, why are there still families of eight or nine people in the world who can live together lovingly and harmoniously under one roof?

Everyone says that people are selfish and that the world is difficult. We only see that everyone always wants to deceive others and is unwilling to be deceived. Everything of their own is always raised very high, and everything of others is always depreciated very low, and even the smallest thing in the world must take a lot of effort to succeed. But where do marriages, contracts, peace, armistice agreements, mutual agreements, and all alliances in the world come from?

Small Monographs

From the "Small Army" Theory to the "Total War" Theory 185

— Zhang Shaochuan

After the last World War, the most popular theory in the study of tactics was the so-called "small army" theory. People such as Fuller of England, Douhet of Italy, and Seeckt of Germany were all famous military commentators, but they were also advocates of the "small army" theory. According to them, in future wars, it would be unnecessary to arm the entire nation or the broad masses of the people; because with the development of weapons and the advancement of military technology, it would only be necessary to use a small corps equipped with the latest weapons to penetrate deep into the enemy's territory, deliver a devastating blow, and victory could be achieved. Douhet believed that as long as fifteen hundred bombers carrying five or six thousand tons of bombs were used to destroy the enemy's air force bases, seize air supremacy, and deliver a devastating blow to the heart of the enemy country, the issue of victory or defeat would be resolved. Fuller advocated using a mechanized small army of ten thousand men, carrying two thousand tanks, four hundred motorized artillery pieces, and hundreds of aircraft to break through the enemy's lines, invade the enemy country, in order to seize victory and end the war. The famous Italian assault warfare theorist Amedeo Mecozzi also believed that "the key to surprise" had a decisive effect on the war situation, and therefore he advocated using a small army to invade the enemy's rear to achieve victory. From the perspective of such a "small army" theory, future wars would not be protracted, nor would they involve great sacrifices; in fact, the advocates of the "small army" theory often told the general public: future wars would only require a small number of elite troops, and would achieve victory through "surprise attacks" in a very short period of time, so they would definitely not be as cruel as the last World War.

Such a "small army" theory was of course not conjured out of thin air by those military commentators; its emergence was based on certain social foundations. This can be explained in the following points.

First, during the World War of 1914-18, the people of many capitalist countries awakened and turned around, causing those countries to experience serious domestic wars, almost resulting in the end of capitalism. After the end of the war, the imperialist powers, in order to compete for markets, prepared even more actively for the Second World War; but on the other hand, they were afraid of the "unfortunate" events that occurred in the last war repeating themselves, so they did not dare to arm the entire nation, and created the "small army" theory; at the same time, they also told everyone: the Second World War would definitely be short in duration, and would not be as cruel as the last World War, attempting to deceive everyone, so that people's anti-war thoughts would be shaken.

Second, the Treaty of Versailles, established after the war, stipulated on the one hand that countries such as Germany and Austria could not rearm, and on the other hand created a powerful force within the Versailles system: this made those military commentators believe that a total mobilization war between imperialists would not occur; even if a world war did occur, it would only be a mechanized "small army" assault war, and a war mobilizing the entire country was not really necessary. At the same time, the theory of "small army" assaults on strongholds, aggression against colonies, and attacks on new countries arose in response to the times.

Third, the emergence of the "small army" theory also had a deep relationship with the national conditions of certain countries. For example, Douhet's theory of aerial warfare originated from Italy, which was inferior to other imperialist powers in all aspects. Because Italy's economy and military were more backward compared to countries such as Britain and France; at the same time, its position was also relatively unfavorable, and the so-called "prisoner of the Mediterranean" was its title; therefore, Douhet created his theory in an attempt to use the latest military technology—aircraft—to save and develop Italy. Also, Fuller's proposition was also suitable for Britain's special situation. Because the British Empire possessed vast colonies around the world, it was impossible for it to use a large army to protect them; what was important to it was the navy and air force; and Fuller's proposition was precisely for this point.

However, the current situation is completely different. With the development of contradictions between the powers, the competition for military expansion among countries, and the destruction of international treaties, not only has the issue of the Second World War become increasingly realistic, but also in various facts it has been made clear that this war will inevitably be more cruel than the last one, and the strength between the belligerent countries will inevitably be stronger, and the so-called "small army" theory has already gone bankrupt in practice. Now, both Germany and Italy, the birthplaces of this theory, are in total mobilization, and no one will pay attention to that kind of "small army" theory anymore. Facts tell us: Germany has created an army of more than a million; once a war breaks out, not only all men, but also all women will be mobilized. As for Italy, when it launched its expedition to East Africa, it actually mobilized an army of more than a million; last year, Italy also stipulated that citizens should receive military education from the age of eight; Mussolini recently made a public and boastful declaration to the world, saying that once something happens, Italy can mobilize an army of more than eight million in a short period of time! In addition, countries such as Poland, France, Britain, and Japan are also working hard on total mobilization. In this way, the so-called "small army" theory has been replaced by "total war."

The so-called "total war" is the highest expression of the military wisdom of militarism. In the current Germany, Italy, and other militarist countries, books discussing "total war" are very popular. The so-called "annihilation war," "war science," "total war," and "total victory" are the most fashionable topics of Hitler and Mussolini's military spokespersons. At the same time, in German and Italian schools, professors of certain subjects mostly lecture students on "total war" and related theories. In this way, "total war" has become inseparable from the current political system in Germany and Italy.

So, what is the meaning of "total war"? What is its content? According to the explanations of military commentators in Germany, Italy, and other countries, it is: first, not only to send the entire country's army to the battlefield, but also to have the entire nation participate in the war, not only to carry out military mobilization, but also to have the economic and "spiritual" total mobilization of the entire nation; second, occupying a certain place is not for political purposes, but for the purpose of completely annihilating the enemy; third, "total war" is a war conducted with the determination to fight to the death, using all possible means, without limitation and without forgiveness. Ludendorff, the author of "Total War," said: "...During the World War, the belligerent countries had to wage war in a combat zone of several kilometers; like the war itself, it would exhaust the residents near the war zone; in this complete sense, the battlefield would inevitably expand to the entire territory of the belligerent countries. Not only the army, but also the people must directly participate in the war, although their participation differs somewhat in form and degree. ...Total war, not only for the armed forces, but also for the nation, must directly conduct war. ...Total war will actually pose a fatal threat to the entire nation...." This is the essence of "total war."

Regarding the issue of the relationship between war and politics, theorists of "total war" also have special explanations. For example, Ludendorff argued:

"...The essence of war has changed, the essence of politics has changed, and thus the political relationship for military guidance has also changed. ...War and politics are used to maintain the life of the nation, and war is an even higher expression of the nation's desire to survive. Therefore, politics must serve the guidance of the military." According to his argument, both domestic and foreign politics must serve war, and in this regard there is the so-called "total politics."

On this issue of the relationship between war and politics, although the opinions of military commentators have some differences, they are all equally devoted to supporting "total war" and "total politics."

As for the significance of victory in "total war," according to those military commentators, it lies in completely and permanently conquering the enemy and enslaving other nations. One "total war" theorist said: "The future war will not only be total in the sense of the use of force, but also in the far-reaching nature of the results. In other words, the total victory means the total destruction of the loser, which is the complete and thorough elimination of the defeated from the historical arena of competition. ...In this kind of war, there are only victors and vanquished, only survivors and nations that are removed from the national register. This war does not end by legal means, but by the cessation of military action in fact. ..." According to this statement, if the general public does not rise up to fight for the imperialists desperately, then their nation will be in danger of being permanently eliminated: this is obviously a deliberate exaggeration by the militarists, attempting to incite their people to rise up and fight for them, to conquer others and enslave other nations.

However, no matter what, "total war" always has great inherent dangers; that is, in the total mobilization of the entire nation, in the development and prolongation of a cruel war, the majority of the people in the aggressor countries will inevitably gradually awaken, use the weapons given to them by the aggressors to oppose the war of aggression, and to strive for their own freedom and liberation, in order to achieve permanent human harmony. Such a terrible event was something that the imperialists experienced during the last World War.

Page 19

Therefore, while they are singing the "songs of total war," on the other hand they are also raising the issue of the organization of the wartime army and the thinking of the army and the general public. They advocate incorporating the sons of wealthy families and soldiers who have received strict training in peacetime into ordinary troops to play a leading role, and also advocate using various effective methods to publicize and train ordinary soldiers, so that they can resolutely fight for the motherland and to forever conquer others in order to gain final victory. At the same time, they also implement strict surveillance and oppression of the general public. The aforementioned Ludendorff once openly shouted: "Of course, the state, that is, the military leadership of total politics and total war, must adopt special measures. For example, strict review of newspapers and magazines, strict laws to maintain military secrets, sealing off borders connecting with neutral countries, prohibiting gatherings, and at least arresting the heads of 'dissenting factions,' and strictly monitoring railway transportation and wireless telephone broadcasts." However, people strive for their own interests and for the truth they believe in; we believe that even under the severe oppression and various deceptions of imperialism, the majority of their people will not forget their own interests and the truth they should know: therefore, in the development of "total war," the majority of the people of imperialism will inevitably experience greater suffering and greater resistance, and the crisis of imperialism will naturally be even greater.

Thus, the development from "small army" to "total war" can be said to be the development of the imperialist aggression, and at the same time it is the development of their crisis.

Timely Articles

Gazing at Chang'e Through a Telescope: Talking About the Moon During Mid-Autumn Festival 186

— Ling

Among all the Chinese festivals, the Mid-Autumn Festival is probably the most interesting and poetic; although according to folklore researchers, the commemoration of the Mid-Autumn Festival originated from "killing the Tatars," it has completely become a day to worship the moon god.

The moon, in the eyes of most people, is indeed a very mysterious thing. In various countries around the world, there are all kinds of stories and legends about the moon, and these legends and stories are more beautiful and gentle than those of other festivals. Just in our country, some say that in that jade palace in the heavens there lives a beautiful woman who stole the elixir of immortality, named Chang'e; others say that there is only a rabbit living there, whose job is to pound medicine day and night; others say that there is also an old man there chopping cassia trees. As for the West, some say that there is a goddess who makes a living by hunting, riding deer and galloping on the icy and flawless moon all day long; others say that there are flocks of sheep on the moon, giant crabs, and young girls reading books, and so on. People on Earth often hope to go and see this mysterious place, so in legends there are beautiful stories such as Emperor Ming of Tang visiting the Moon Palace. In my hometown, there is also the custom of "watching the moon's radiance" during the Mid-Autumn Festival, saying that at midnight, when all is silent, the Moon Palace opens with a bang, and colorful carriages emerge in single file, as the princess is being married off to another planet; those who see this grand wedding will surely have great luck.

In fact, if we had such a high ladder that we could climb onto the moon to take a look, these wonderful illusions would be immediately shattered.

The moon is only three hundred eighty-four, three hundred ninety-five kilometers away from the earth, which is connecting thirty Earths in a row, or taking a path circling the Earth ten times as long, one can reach the moon. However, our naked eyes cannot clearly see things at such a long distance, so even on the Mid-Autumn Festival night, when the air is clearest and the moonlight is brightest, we can only see a round jade plate emitting a gentle blue light; looking more closely, we can only see some black patches on it that resemble various figures; rationally and reasonably, the legends of beauties, rabbits, deer, and so on in the Moon Palace must have come from imagining these black patches.

So, what exactly are these black patches?

Professor Pickering, an authority on lunar research, once used the world's largest telescope at the Wilson Mountain Observatory in the United States to take a large photograph of the moon's surface with a diameter of thirty inches. From this photograph, we see that the moon is not only not as smooth as jade or a mirror, but also uneven, with seas, mountains, valleys, and countless round holes; however, these seas, mountains, holes, and valleys are not as beautiful as those on our Earth. Because there is no air or dust on the moon, the places hit by sunlight will not reflect, and apart from those places that dazzle the eyes, the rest of the area is as dark as if it were in the middle of the night. From the Earth, it was originally such a bright and pure round moon, but when it loses the sunlight, it becomes a dark mass. Moreover, there is no water on the moon, so there are no changeable clouds, and even if there are high mountains, there are no rushing waterfalls, and even if there are valleys, there are no trickling streams. As for the scene of vast plains, misty and foggy, with mountains and wild grasses like carpets, that is even more non-existent. How monotonous! How desolate! Some say that even during the day on the moon, its temperature is still below freezing, and even if there is a small amount of water, it would have frozen into ice and snow long ago; the white, hazy thing we see on the moon's surface in our telescopes may be the covering of ice and snow. Also, if we really had the ability to fly to the moon with two or three friends, but because there is no air on the moon, we would lose the medium for sound transmission, and we could not hear each other even if we spoke face to face.

Continued on the Fifth Edition

Page 20

Page 21

Everyone would suddenly become mute. In addition to this difficulty, there is also the danger of being hit by meteors at all times; these meteors sometimes also fall on the Earth, but because there is a thick layer of air surrounding the Earth, when a meteor falls, this layer of air reduces its momentum a lot, and it collides with the air, forcing it to split into many fragments, and then the danger is avoided; but on the moon, these meteors, without any obstacles, fall down like artillery shells without any mercy.

On this icy and snowy moon, since there are no rivers or trees, living things certainly cannot grow, so on the moon, apart from rocks, caves, and high mountains, there is almost nothing. Some scholars say that many years ago, the moon was also alive like the Earth, and could produce all things, but now it is dead—completely dead—the light it emits is not actually its own light, and if we carefully analyze this gentle light, we can know that its color is exactly the same as sunlight; this shows that moonlight is just the light reflected from the sun. But why is moonlight not as strong as sunlight? This is because it does not reflect all of the sunlight, but only one-tenth of it.

The Mid-Autumn Festival of the 25th year of the Republic of China has arrived again. Now that we know all the sights on the moon, we should no longer be deceived by the illusions of those black patches, right?

Amateur Coffee House

Pure Discussion and Idle Talk 187

— Fei

It seems that historically, whenever a nation faces times of turmoil, a segment of scholars, intellectuals, and literati invariably engages in "pure discussion," expressing dissatisfaction with the current state, whether through direct remonstrance or indirect satire. Conversely, others engage in "idle talk." Naturally, they too are dissatisfied with the status quo, but they adopt a passive attitude, remaining indifferent to national affairs, spending their days drinking wine, composing poetry, and wandering among mountains and rivers. Later generations have offered many commentaries on these two types of people. Regarding the former, some say they were able to disregard the threat of punishment and devote themselves to national affairs, while others say they were asking for trouble and acting unnecessarily. Regarding the latter, some say they only sought to "preserve their own purity," disregarding important national matters and thus failing to be true men, while others say they were capable of "avoiding danger and disaster," and could be considered "reclusive scholars."

However, regardless of the debate, those who engaged in "pure discussion" continued to do so, and those who engaged in "idle talk" continued to do so. But as far as we know, idle talk was indeed more advantageous than pure discussion. Idle talkers, of course, sometimes, in their conversations, couldn't completely suppress their inner resentment, and inadvertently revealed a bit of "misanthropy and cynicism," which could lead to execution. But for the most part, as long as you were "cautious and careful," you could always "preserve your head" or "live out your days as a farmer." But those who engaged in pure discussion did not have it so easy. Among them, if you were truly engaged in "pure" discussion, and not "turbid" discussion, then rarely would you avoid being "thrown into the turbid waters along with your kind." The most obvious example is the Donglin Party of the Ming Dynasty. Precisely because of this, the number of people engaging in pure discussion gradually decreased, and precisely because of this, the number of people engaging in idle talk gradually increased.

Everyone knows that the Seven Sages of the Bamboo Grove of the Jin Dynasty, such as Ji Kang, Ruan Ji, and Liu Ling, were the founding fathers of our idle talk circles. Some of them indulged in wine and women, while others immersed themselves in poetry and prose. Generally, when they met, they would always boast and chat. What they talked about was nothing more than literary compositions, drunken women, or impersonal topics such as "the vastness of the heavens and earth, the insignificance of a fly." Their words were "incoherent and illogical," and their behavior was "unrestrained," seeming drunk, foolish, crazy, and mad. People like this were truly "doing nothing." If the whole country were like this, then no one would be doing anything, and it would truly be "idle talk ruining the country!"

Strangely enough, since you cannot engage in "pure discussion," then you should be well-behaved, eat your food, wear your clothes, and sleep your sleep. Why must you nag and chatter? Sometimes, unintentionally, you not only fail to entertain the country, but also endanger your own life, which is truly incomplete. We seem to remember that Ji Kang was also "beheaded in the marketplace" because of careless words, right? You pretended to be crazy and talked nonsense. The country was originally "as secure as a rock," but after your actions, which seemed to be spreading rumors and organizing conspiracies, wasn't the country ruined by you?

Furthermore, rulers throughout history have always been protective of their shortcomings and pleased by flattery. Even ordinary people are like this. If you can engage in idle talk, and your idle talk can become a common practice, then such a person must not be ordinary. The country will always be able to use someone like you. You must gloss over the faults of the court, or at least sit and eat your salary, remaining silent and taciturn, so that he can feel at ease with you. If you deliberately want to express "high-flying and far-reaching," "preserving your own purity," then you are satirizing the monarch in your actions, which is tantamount to considering yourself "pure" and him "turbid." Just this alone has planted the seeds of sin, let alone engaging in pure discussion? Because "I am the state," anything detrimental to the emperor is considered ruining the country, and therefore the crime is unforgivable.

However, a person who likes to talk, and since he is human, how can he not "talk"? Farmers can talk about the weather, droughts and floods, rice, sorghum, and millet. Merchants can talk about business, whether buying and selling is good, and whether a certain business is good to do. So what do scholars and literati talk about? Poetry and lyrics are naturally one of the topics they talk about, but just talking about this is still idle talk, isn't it? Moreover, scholars throughout history have all spoken of "serving in the government after excelling in learning," so after studying well, they will naturally talk about serving in the government, and therefore also talk about national affairs. In the active sense, it is expressed as pure discussion, and in the passive sense, it is expressed as idle talk. In short, it's just talking after all. Scholars always have to talk. Although such talk cannot be said to save the country, in reality, how can it be enough to ruin the country?

In reality, regardless of whether idle talk ruins the country or not, once there is idle talk within a country, and idle talk becomes a common practice, becoming fashionable for a time, then the country always feels a bit uneasy, and the country always feels a bit ruined, ruined by figures like Wu Sangui. Therefore, some people may only see the phenomenon and not see the essence, and insist on reversing cause and effect, stubbornly saying "idle talk ruins the country," without asking whether the country was ruined first and then there was idle talk, or whether the country was ruined after there was idle talk.

If idle talk is sure to ruin the country, then wouldn't many street rumors also ruin the country? Aren't those who sit in teahouses drinking tea all day also people who ruin the country? Do we have to remain silent after tea and wine? From this, we can understand that idle talk still has a scope, and the words spoken in idle talk also have a certain content. It takes certain idle talk to avoid the qualification of ruining the country, that is, "don't talk about national affairs, only talk about the wind, flowers, snow, and moon."

Now is also an era when idle talk is popular, but the techniques of idle talk are more advanced than before. Perhaps this is a collection of the great achievements of idle talk from ancient and modern times, both Chinese and foreign? But at this time, idle talk will definitely not have the suspicion of ruining the country, and it can't be said to have the qualification of ruining the country either. Street rumors and boasting after tea and wine go without saying, while the literati of the present time rack their brains to come up with many methods of idle talk. After meeting, in addition to things like "the weather today... ha ha ha," there are movie stars, dancing stars, box murder cases, etc. to talk about, without having to involve national affairs. As for writers who are not content with silence, they can also compile small literary magazines like Analects, Lost Classics, and Cosmic Wind to write some humorous articles, which is also equivalent to engaging in idle talk. This will definitely not ruin the country, and there is no fear that the whole world will be a family of idle talkers. At the same time, precisely because these idle talks are not idle talks that ruin the country, then the country will not be ruined.

But what is worrying is that if the country is ever ruined—although not due to idle talk—when it is ruined by figures like Yin Rugeng, then how will these non-ruining idle talkers save the already ruined country?

Introduction to "Contemporary International Celebrities" 188

— You Yu

Compiled by Ge Qiao, sold by Life Bookstore, special price of seven jiao per volume

In the turbulent international situation, the famous figures active on the world political stage are truly worthy of special attention. Because the words and deeds of these figures often represent the attitudes of those in power or those in opposition in certain countries towards the general situation, and world peace.
